• I reviewed all seven files. The live JSONs already contain the five governance sections and the newer step fields, so
  the biggest problem is no longer “missing v3.2 features”; it is drift, contradiction, and stale analysis around the
  current state.

  Critical

  - The artifact-containment contract is internally inconsistent. The template says all artifacts must live
    under .acms_runs/{run_id}/, but the same template hard-codes audit, run-status, and mutation-ledger outputs
    under .state/..., and artifact_root_baseline explicitly allows both .state/ and .acms_runs/. The instruction doc
    then says both “map .state/ paths to the run root pattern” and “store artefacts and evidence under .state/”. This
    leaves run containment undefined. See Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1639,
    Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1661, Gov_Reg/

    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1834, and Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_INSTRUCTION_DOCUMENT_V3_2.json:7.

  High

  - Cross-platform support is overstated. The template claims Windows/Linux/macOS support, but the default shell is
    bash, and the worktree/gate commands rely on POSIX test, grep, pipes, and && without OS-specific variants. That is
    not a credible Windows-default contract. See Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:399,

• I reviewed all seven files. The live JSONs already contain the five governance sections and the newer step fields, so
  the biggest problem is no longer “missing v3.2 features”; it is drift, contradiction, and stale analysis around the
  current state.

  Critical

  - The artifact-containment contract is internally inconsistent. The template says all artifacts must live
  under .acms_runs/{run_id}/, but the same template hard-codes audit, run-status, and mutation-ledger outputs
  under .state/..., and artifact_root_baseline explicitly allows both .state/ and .acms_runs/. The instruction doc then
  says both “map .state/ paths to the run root pattern” and “store artefacts and evidence under .state/”. This leaves
  run containment undefined. See Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1639, Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1661, Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1790, Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1815, Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1834, and Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_INSTRUCTION_DOCUMENT_V3_2.json:7.

  High

  - Cross-platform support is overstated. The template claims Windows/Linux/macOS support, but the default shell is
  bash, and the worktree/gate commands rely on POSIX test, grep, pipes, and && without OS-specific variants. That is not
  a credible Windows-default contract. See Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:399,
  Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:428, Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1761, and Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:934.
  - The technical spec has major version/path drift. Its metadata title still says v3.0.0 while the document version is
  3.2.0; plan_document.root_structure still describes the layout as “Template v3.0.0”; many template_path entries point
  to legacy ...TEMPLATE_V3.json or updated_...V3_1.json; the appendix still references
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3.json and AI_AGENT_INSTRUCTIONS.md. See Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:4, Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:687, Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:737, Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:845, and Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:2454.
  - The spec’s lower-level data-structure documentation lags the template. execution_patterns in the template includes
  pattern_validation and guardrail_policy, but the spec’s data_structures.execution_patterns omits them. traceability in
  the template includes gap_to_execution_packet, deferred_gaps, and gap_closure_validation, but the spec omits those
  too. See Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1578, Gov_Reg/

• The two Markdown evaluations point to one combined change set: move the system from “pattern-aware” to “pattern-
  governed and configuration-driven.” The current template/spec already have partial support in Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:37, Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:17, and Gov_Reg/
  NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_INSTRUCTION_DOCUMENT_V3_2.json:7, but they still leave a loophole for null/blank pattern binding
  and prose-driven behavior. The plan below folds in both [ChatGPT-Template Feature Validation.md](C:
  \Users\richg\Gov_Reg\ChatGPT-Template Feature Validation.md) and [ChatGPT-Configuration-Driven Development
  Evaluation.md](C:\Users\richg\Gov_Reg\ChatGPT-Configuration-Driven Development Evaluation.md) without creating
  duplicate semantics.

  Plan

  1. Define the unified model before editing any file.

  - Add three canonical top-level concepts: pattern_governance, configuration_driven_development, and executor_registry.
  - Fold pattern_resolution_phase, pattern_creation_contract, and manual_exception_policy under pattern_governance
    instead of scattering them as separate peers.
  - Keep existing pattern_id and pattern_parameters, but extend executable-step binding with implementation_mode,
    executor_binding, behavior_spec, allowed_extension_slots, bespoke_logic_allowed, and behavior_binding_proof.
  - Use the six GATE-CFG-* gates as the canonical gate set, and document that they satisfy the three pattern-gate
    requirements from the template validation memo so you do not end up with redundant gate registries.

  2. Update the autonomous delivery template first, because it is the concrete contract surface.

  - In Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:37, strengthen critical_constraint.rules to
    forbid patternless execution, null pattern IDs on executable steps, ad hoc behavior sources, and unregistered
    executors.
  - Add new top-level sections for pattern_governance, configuration_driven_development, and executor_registry.
  - Extend Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:98 with pattern-resolution outputs such as
    existing_pattern_match, new_pattern_required, executor_family, and config_driven_feasibility.
  - Extend Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:202 so each file entry can declare pattern
    provenance and whether it is a pattern artifact, pattern output, or approved manual exception.
  - Extend Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:671 so executable steps require executor/
    config/spec binding, while PATTERN_CREATION and NOT_AUTOMATABLE remain the only exceptions.
  - Extend Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:912, Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1563, Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1569, Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1575, Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1613, and Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1868 with the new CDD fields, triggers, and evidence
    requirements.
  - Rewrite Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1524 so they explicitly prohibit blank
    pattern_id, prompt-only behavior binding, bespoke scripts where a registered pattern exists, and implementation
    before pattern creation/validation.

  3. Update the technical specification second so the semantics match the template.

  - In Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:17, add configuration-driven development as a
    design principle and add executor-binding / behavior-binding proof to key capabilities.
  - In Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:60, add Pattern Registry, Executor Registry,
    Configuration Schema Validator, Behavior Binding Validator, Pattern Creation Workflow, and CDD Enforcement Gates.
  - In Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:684, add the new top-level sections so the spec
    matches the template.
  - In Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:969, add the new executable-step fields and change
    pattern_id from optional reference semantics to mandatory binding semantics for executable steps.
  - Reframe Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:1208, expand Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:1198, Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:1248, and Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:1380, and replace executor_function as the sole binding
    primitive with executor_id plus config/schema/output-contract requirements.

  4. Update the instruction document last, because it is stored as one JSON string and depends on the final section
     names.

  - In Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_INSTRUCTION_DOCUMENT_V3_2.json:7, replace the current “identify the gap / allow null
    pattern_id” guidance with “create and validate a pattern before any implementation planning.”
  - Add a front-loaded PATTERN-FIRST / CONFIGURATION-DRIVEN execution law near the current NO IMPLIED BEHAVIOR guidance.
  - Update the instructions for task_analysis, execution_patterns, step_contracts, and pipeline_boundary_contract so the
    executable task without a validated pattern binding.
  - Edit this file as plain text first, then serialize back into the JSON content string; hand-editing escaped newlines
  - Confirm executor_function is no longer the sole binding primitive anywhere.
  - Confirm the gate names, allowed execution inputs, traceability fields, and AI prohibitions are identical across
    template, spec, and instruction doc.

• Overall
  The alternate response is broadly aligned with the plan I created. It identifies the same root change: move the system
  from permissive pattern usage to enforced pattern-first, configuration-driven execution. Relative to my plan, it is
  more operational and release-oriented, but also more speculative and less tightly grounded in the current file state.

  Where It’s Strong

  - It correctly treats the two evaluation docs as complementary rather than conflicting, and unifies them under one
    core principle at Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-donut.md:5.
  - It adds more implementation discipline than my plan: explicit mod IDs, per-file sequencing, and instruction-document
    handling notes at Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-donut.md:16 and Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-donut.md:178.
  - Its versioning and migration suggestions are grounded in real spec sections. The technical spec already has
    gate_registry, version_history, and migration_guide at Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:167 and Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:2500, so its release-management additions are structurally
    plausible.
  - It also correctly notices editable template metadata and AI intake instructions that can absorb the new governance
    behavior at Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:2 and Gov_Reg/
    NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1525.

  Where It’s Weaker Or Riskier Than My Plan

  - It forces a v3.3.0 upgrade across all three files at Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-donut.md:10 and Gov_Reg/greedy-
    toasting-donut.md:71. My plan avoided that because the user asked for incorporation, not a release/versioning
    change. This is scope inflation unless you explicitly want a breaking revision.
  - It uses Unix-style verification guidance on a Windows workspace: > /dev/null at Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-donut.md:24.
    That is not environment-correct here.
  - It changes the registry path to registry/pattern_registry.yaml at Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-donut.md:107 and Gov_Reg/
    greedy-toasting-donut.md:126, but the actual repo search turned up Gov_Reg/MINI_PIPE/patterns/PATTERN_INDEX.yaml,
    not that path. My plan deliberately did not canonicalize a registry path without evidence.
  - It says to replace execution_patterns at Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-donut.md:122. That is riskier than my “extend,
    don’t replace” approach because the current template already has working pattern_validation and guardrail_policy
    structure at Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json:1575.
  - It introduces an internal inconsistency: pre_execution_gate is GATE_PATTERN_BINDING at Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-
    donut.md:110, but the actual gate set it proposes is GATE-CFG-001 through GATE-CFG-006 at Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-
    donut.md:118. My plan explicitly folded the pattern gates into the GATE-CFG-* family to avoid this.
  - It misses one major item from the evaluation docs that my plan included: file_manifest needs pattern-aware
    provenance rules. In its template section from Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-donut.md:77 through Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-
    donut.md:174, there is no file_manifest modification.
  - Its gate-count math is stale. It proposes changing GATE-003’s “13 required fields” to “21” at Gov_Reg/greedy-
    toasting-donut.md:42, but the current step-contract schema already contains 21 required fields under the plan
    document model at Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json:969. If you add 7 more CDD fields,
    the new total would need to be higher, not 21.
  - Its pipeline_boundary_contract expansion is partial at Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-donut.md:144. It omits
    validated_parameter_object and the explicit forbid_prompt_only_behavior_binding rule that the CDD evaluation called
    for and that my plan preserved.
  - It adds engine_invariants at Gov_Reg/greedy-toasting-donut.md:159, which may be useful, but it is not clearly
    sourced from either evaluation document or the current schema. My plan stayed closer to the requested changes.

  Comparison Verdict
  If you want a high-level, schema-aware modification plan with less speculative scope, my plan is stronger. If you want
  a more implementation-ready checklist with release-management detail, the alternate response is stronger.

  The best merged approach would be:

  - Keep the alternate response’s explicit mod-by-mod structure and migration/version-history awareness.
  - Keep my plan’s scope control, deduplication, and file-grounded corrections.
  - Do not adopt its version bump, registry-path change, execution_patterns replacement, or gate-count math as written.
  - Add the missing file_manifest provenance changes and explicit pattern_resolution_phase before using it as the
    working edit plan.

  If you want, I can turn both into one corrected final edit plan and then apply the JSON changes.

› what do these changes do?


• These changes harden the planning system from “structured and validated” to “pattern-constrained and fail-closed.”

  Right now, v3.2 governs the work well: phases, steps, evidence, gates, traceability. The gap identified in the plans
  is that an agent can still reach implementation with too much freehand behavior: a nullable pattern_id, a vague
  executor reference, or prompt-only logic. The proposed edits close that gap.

  What they do in practice:

  - They add three new governance surfaces: pattern_governance, configuration_driven_development, and executor_registry.
  - They replace a loose binding like executor_function with a stricter contract: executor identity plus config/schema/
    output references.
  - They forbid “just implement it” behavior when no pattern exists. Instead, the plan must create and validate a new
  - They extend file manifest and anti-pattern detection so the system can detect patternless execution, prompt-only
    behavior binding, and ad hoc logic.

  Net effect: these are not feature changes to an app. They are governance changes to the planning framework itself.
  MERGED_CORRECTED_FINAL_EDIT_PLAN.md keeps the same architectural goal but says to make the minimum safe edits and
  avoid forcing a version bump or registry rename unless that is intentional.

› are these addressed:  Confirmed & New Conflicts

    1. Gate count hardcoded in multiple spec locations

    With all plans applied: 19 (existing) + 6 (GATE-CFG) + 3 (GATE-BEH) + 5 (GATE-CFGCTX) = 33 total gates. But the
  spec
    has hardcoded counts in three separate places none of the upgrade plans address:
    - layer_2_validation component object: total_gates: 19, mandatory_gates: 17
    - Workflow step 9 success criteria: "All 19 validation gates pass"
    - validation_gate_execution_workflow step 4 aggregate: "Total gates: 19"

    FINAL_EDIT_PLAN (S-06) only updates to 25/23. No plan accounts for the Layer 2 +5 gates or updates the workflow
    description strings.

    ---
    2. Both machine plans use fragile positional array pointers (conflicts with indexing plan)

    Both Layer 1 (SPEC-011) and Layer 2 (L2-SPEC-009) append to:
    /architecture/system_layers/layer_2_validation/components/1/gate_registry
    This uses a hardcoded numeric index /1 — exactly what the indexing plan exists to eliminate. If BLK-004 runs first
  and
     reorders components while adding component_id, the index /1 becomes wrong for both patches.

    ---
    3. executor_function — confirmed in both source files

    The current template (execution_patterns.pattern_validation.required_pattern_components, line 1582) and spec
    (execution_patterns.structure.pattern_validation.required_pattern_components, line 1216) both still reference
    executor_function. FINAL_EDIT_PLAN (T-07, S-04) replaces it. The machine plans don't touch this field at all. If
  only
    machine plans are applied, executor_function survives despite the governance goal.

    ---
    4. PATTERN_INDEX.yaml in protected_paths — unaddressed by all plans

    Template protected_paths.paths (line 1852) lists "PATTERN_INDEX.yaml" as a protected file. FINAL_EDIT_PLAN renames
  all
     references to registry/pattern_registry.yaml but no plan updates protected_paths to match. After the rename, the
  old
    protected path silently becomes orphaned protection for a file that no longer exists under that name.

    ---
    5. required_sections universality vs. conditional scope — Layer 2 internal conflict

    Layer 2 spec patch L2-SPEC-003 adds shared_core_architecture_contract, agent_context_contract, and
    compatibility_enforcement_stack to the required_sections array — making them mandatory for all plans. But Layer 2
    instruction patch L2-INST-007 says to add the corresponding gates only "to plans that involve CLI coding agents,
  code
    generation, or code modification" — making them conditional. The spec says always required; the instructions say
  only
    when relevant.

    ---
    6. planning_hierarchy — replace vs. extend (confirmed with actual structure)

    Current template (lines 1563–1568):
    {"system_level": {}, "module_level": [], "component_level": [], "execution_packet_level": []}
    - FINAL_EDIT_PLAN (T-11): replaces the entire object with structured objects containing new fields
    - Layer 1 (TPL-009): merge_object_fields — adds behavior_governance_required, system_level_behavior_profile, etc.
  to
    the existing structure

    If Layer 1 runs first, the merge adds fields to the flat structure. Then FINAL_EDIT_PLAN replaces the whole thing,
    discarding Layer 1's additions.

    ---
    7. execution_patterns replace vs. extend (confirmed with actual structure)

    Current template (lines 1575–1595): has pattern_registry_reference: "PATTERN_INDEX.yaml", executor_function in
    required components.
    - FINAL_EDIT_PLAN (T-07): "replace the entire object value"
    - MERGED_CORRECTED: "extend it, not replace"
    - Layer 1 (TPL-006, TPL-007, TPL-008): uses merge_object_fields and extend_array_item_schema_example
    - Layer 2 (L2-TPL-006): also uses merge_object_fields

    Three plans extend, one replaces. If the replace runs last it wipes the other plans' additions; if it runs first,
  the
    merges apply on top but the starting point is already the replaced version.

    ---
    8. GATE-008 duplicate confirmed (BLK-001)

    Spec lines 249–259 show two separate objects both with "id": "GATE-008" — one named "Automation Spec" and one named
    "Automation Index". Both Layer 1 and Layer 2 append to this same gate_registry using the /1 positional pointer. If
  the
     blocker fix renumbers or reorders entries first, those pointers break. If the v3.3 patches run first, they append
  on
    top of the still-duplicate array.

• I’m collapsing the matrix into a single decision document now: one ruling per conflict, plus the exact execution order
  those rulings imply.

• Resolved Authority Spec

  Rulings below define the no-ambiguity mainline.

  1. The work is split into two phases. Phase A is blocker remediation on the live v3.2 JSONs, driven by Gov_Reg/
     guardrails_template_project/plansforthis/plansforthis/cli_blocker_fix_guide.md and Gov_Reg/
     guardrails_template_project/plansforthis/plansforthis/final_indexing_implementation_plan.json. Phase B is the
     optional governance migration, driven primarily by Gov_Reg/guardrails_template_project/plansforthis/plansforthis/
     MERGED_CORRECTED_FINAL_EDIT_PLAN.md.
  2. The machine style and machine layer-2 patch plans are excluded from the mainline. Use Gov_Reg/
     guardrails_template_project/plansforthis/plansforthis/v3_3_patch_plan_machine_style.json and Gov_Reg/
     guardrails_template_project/plansforthis/plansforthis/v3_3_patch_plan_machine_layer2.json only as alternate
     branches or idea sources, not as additive patches.
  3. Edit order for any governance migration is spec, then template, then instruction document. That follows Gov_Reg/
     guardrails_template_project/plansforthis/plansforthis/MERGED_CORRECTED_FINAL_EDIT_PLAN.md, not the template-first
     order from the other plans.
  4. The canonical governance gate family is GATE-CFG-001 through GATE-CFG-006 only. GATE-BEH-* and GATE-CFGCTX-* are
     not part of the mainline.
  5. Gate counts and gate-count prose must be derived from the adopted gate family only. In Phase A, the spec remains at
     the current 19-gate model until blocker fixes are done. In Phase B, if only GATE-CFG-001..006 are added, counts
     become 25 total and 23 mandatory, and all hardcoded strings such as “All 19 validation gates pass” and “Total
     gates: 19” must be updated in the same pass. The live count anchors are in Gov_Reg/
     NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json.
  6. The registry path stays PATTERN_INDEX.yaml unless a separate explicit migration approves a rename. This follows
     Gov_Reg/guardrails_template_project/plansforthis/plansforthis/MERGED_CORRECTED_FINAL_EDIT_PLAN.md and the live
     template at Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json.
  7. Because the registry path is not being renamed by default, protected_paths.paths continues to protect
     PATTERN_INDEX.yaml. If a later path migration is approved, protected_paths must be updated atomically in that same
     change set.
  8. Versioning is phase-based. Phase A remains in the v3.2 line and does not declare 3.3.0. If Phase B is adopted with
     the breaking pattern-first rules, that release is 3.3.0.
  9. No patch plan may rely on positional array pointers like /architecture/system_layers/layer_2_validation/
     components/1/gate_registry once Phase A begins. All gate-registry targeting must be rewritten to use stable
     semantic resolution after BLK-004 is addressed.
  10. BLK-001 is mandatory first: resolve the duplicate GATE-008 in the live spec before any gate-registry append or
     renumbering work. The duplicate is present in Gov_Reg/NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json.
  11. BLK-004 is mandatory before adding new system-layer components. Any component appended to
     architecture.system_layers.*.components must include a unique component_id from the moment it is introduced. If the
     “CDD Control Plane” idea is later adopted from Gov_Reg/guardrails_template_project/plansforthis/plansforthis/
     FINAL_EDIT_PLAN_V3_2_TO_V3_3.md, it must be augmented with component_id.
  12. execution_patterns is extended in place, not replaced wholesale. This is the mainline ruling. During Phase B,
     executor_function must be removed from required pattern components and replaced with the approved compound binding
     model. Until Phase B, the live v3.2 references remain as current-state truth in Gov_Reg/
     NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_AUTONOMOUS_DELIVERY_TEMPLATE_V3_2.json and Gov_Reg/
     NEWPHASEPLANPROCESS_TECHNICAL_SPECIFICATION_V3_2.json.
  13. planning_hierarchy is evolved in place. Do not replace the whole object. Extend the existing structure and array
     item schemas without discarding prior fields.
  14. The canonical Phase B step-binding additions are implementation_mode, executor_binding, behavior_spec,
     behavior_binding_proof, allowed_extension_slots, and bespoke_logic_allowed. behavior_binding is not adopted as the
     primary mainline contract.
  15. The layer-2 required-sections model is not adopted in the mainline. Its internal contradiction between global
     required_sections and conditional instruction applicability is resolved by excluding that branch entirely.
  16. The current v3.2 permissive wording around missing patterns remains in force during Phase A only. In Phase B,
     executable steps may no longer use null or blank pattern_id, and that rule is treated as a breaking semantic
     change.

  Execution Sequence

  1. Fix BLK-001 duplicate gate identity.
  2. Fix BLK-002 enhancement IDs.
  3. Resolve BLK-003 execution_phases classification.
  4. Fix BLK-004 component_id gaps.
  5. Validate the index-safe v3.2 baseline.
  6. Decide explicitly whether Phase B is in scope.
  7. If Phase B is approved, apply governance edits in spec → template → instruction order using the merged corrected
     plan as the primary authority.
  8. In that same Phase B pass, update gate counts and prose, remove executor_function, and validate that only the GATE-
     CFG-* family was introduced.

› The document is solid — all 9 matrix conflicts are resolved, the 3 additional gaps I found are addressed, and the
    rulings are internally consistent. Four things worth flagging before you treat this as final:

    ---
    1. BLK-003 resolution is still open

    Ruling 1 assigns BLK-003 to Phase A, and execution step 3 says "resolve BLK-003 execution_phases classification" —
  but
     neither the ruling nor the cli_blocker_fix_guide makes the actual design call. The guide presents two options:
    classify as structural (replace-whole-array, no indexing) or convert to objects with phase_id. Someone needs to
  choose
     before Phase A can complete. Suggest adding a ruling: BLK-003 classifies execution_phases as structural; no
    element-level indexing is needed for that array.

    ---
    2. Phase B needs to specify how MERGED_CORRECTED and FINAL_EDIT_PLAN relate operationally

    Execution step 7 says "using MERGED_CORRECTED as primary authority" but MERGED_CORRECTED is a correction document —
  it
     specifies what not to do and which field names win. The actual edit steps (T-01 through T-17, S-01 through S-10,
  I-01
     through I-14) live in FINAL_EDIT_PLAN. An executor needs to know: run FINAL_EDIT_PLAN steps, constrained by
    MERGED_CORRECTED where they conflict. Suggest making that explicit: FINAL_EDIT_PLAN provides the step sequence;
    MERGED_CORRECTED overrides it at any point of conflict.

    ---
    3. Ruling 9 prohibits positional pointers but doesn't operationalize the rewrite

    The ruling says no positional pointers after Phase A begins. But Phase B's governance edits (S-06 in
  FINAL_EDIT_PLAN)
    target gate_registry — which after BLK-004 will need stable component_id-based resolution, not

  introduced.
     When Phase B adds GATE-CFG-* gates, the affected execution_phases entries are updated by whole-array replacement,

    ---
    Gap 3 — Operationalizing the positional-pointer prohibition

    Recommendation: Make Phase B depend on a completed index resolver, and route all array-element patches through it.

    Concrete ruling to add:
    ▎ Ruling 19. Phase B cannot begin until the locator resolver (scripts/resolve_json_locator.py, indexing plan PH-06)
  is
     operational and the three source files have current indexes/*.index.json artifacts. Any Phase B operation that
    targets an array element (gate_registry, components, section_purpose_map.sections, validation_gates,
    anti_pattern_detection.triggers, etc.) must resolve its target via resolve(file, semantic_id) and apply the patch
    against the resolved pointer at application time. Hand-written /components/1/... paths are rejected during Phase B
    dry-run validation.

    Concrete rewrite recipe for S-06 (spec gate_registry append):

    BEFORE (positional):
      target: /architecture/system_layers/layer_2_validation/components/1/gate_registry

    AFTER (semantic):
      1. Resolve: component_pointer = resolve("spec", "component_id", "COMP-L2-<N>")
                  where N is whatever component_id BLK-004 assigned to Validation Gate System
      2. target: {component_pointer}/gate_registry
      3. Apply append operation
      4. Validate resolved pointer against post-BLK-004 spec before commit

    This makes the rewrite mechanical, not judgment-based. The executor doesn't decide pointers; the index does.
